        French
       </a>
       : Sahara Occidental) is a
       <a href="/wiki/Territorial_dispute" title="Territorial dispute">
        disputed territory
       </a>
       in the
       <a href="/wiki/Maghreb" title="Maghreb">
        Maghreb
       </a>
       region of
       <a href="/wiki/North_Africa" title="North Africa">
        North Africa
       </a>
       , partially controlled by the self-proclaimed
       <a href="/wiki/Sahrawi_Arab_Democratic_Republic" title="Sahrawi Arab Democratic Republic">
        Sahrawi Arab Democratic Republic
       </a>
       and partially Moroccan-
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Occupied_territory" title="Occupied territory">
        occupied
       </a>
       , bordered by
       <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">
        Morocco
       </a>
       proper to the north,
       <a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">
        Algeria
       </a>
       to the northeast,
       <a href="/wiki/Mauritania" title="Mauritania">
        Mauritania
       </a>
       to the east and south, and the
       <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">
        Atlantic Ocean
       </a>
       to the west. Its surface area amounts to 266,000 square kilometres (103,000 sq mi). It is one of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_sovereign_states_and_dependent_territories_by_population_density" title="List of sovereign states and dependent territories by population density">
        most sparsely populated territories in the world
       </a>
       , mainly consisting of desert flatlands. The population is estimated at just over 500,000,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unpop_3-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-unpop-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
       of which nearly 40% live in
       <a href="/wiki/Laayoune" title="Laayoune">
        Laayoune
       </a>
       , the largest city in Western Sahara.
      </p>
      <p>
       Occupied by
       <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">
        Spain
       </a>
       until the late 20th century, Western Sahara has been on the
       <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_list_of_Non-Self-Governing_Territories" title="United Nations list of Non-Self-Governing Territories">
        United Nations list of non-self-governing territories
       </a>
       since 1963 after a Moroccan demand.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-4">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It is the most populous territory on that list, and by far the largest in area. In 1965, the
       <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly" title="United Nations General Assembly">
        UN General Assembly
       </a>
       adopted its first resolution on Western Sahara, asking Spain to decolonise the territory.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       One year later, a new resolution was passed by the General Assembly requesting that a referendum be held by Spain on self-determination.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MINURSO_6-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-MINURSO-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 1975, Spain relinquished the administrative control of the territory to a joint administration by Morocco (which had formally claimed the territory since 1957)
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">
        <a href="#cite_note-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and Mauritania.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MINURSO_6-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-MINURSO-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
       A war erupted between those countries and a
       <a href="/wiki/Sahrawi_people" title="Sahrawi people">
        Sahrawi
       </a>
       nationalist movement, the
       <a href="/wiki/Polisario_Front" title="Polisario Front">
        Polisario Front
       </a>
       , which proclaimed the
       <a href="/wiki/Sahrawi_Arab_Democratic_Republic" title="Sahrawi Arab Democratic Republic">
        Sahrawi Arab Democratic Republic
       </a>
       (SADR) with a
       <a href="/wiki/Government_in_exile" title="Government in exile">
        government in exile
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Tindouf" title="Tindouf">
        Tindouf
       </a>
       , Algeria. Mauritania withdrew its claims in 1979, and Morocco eventually secured
       <i>
        de facto
       </i>
       control of most of the territory, including all the major cities and natural resources. The United Nations considers the Polisario Front to be the legitimate representative of the Sahrawi people, and maintains that the Sahrawis have a right to
       <a href="/wiki/Self-determination" title="Self-determination">
        self-determination
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
        <a href="#cite_note-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Since a
       <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">
        United Nations
       </a>
       -sponsored ceasefire agreement in 1991, two thirds of the territory (including most of the Atlantic coastline - the only part of the coast outside the
       <a href="/wiki/Moroccan_Western_Sahara_Wall" title="Moroccan Western Sahara Wall">
        Moroccan Western Sahara Wall
       </a>
       is the extreme south, including the
       <a href="/wiki/Ras_Nouadhibou" title="Ras Nouadhibou">
        Ras Nouadhibou
       </a>
       peninsula) has been administered by the Moroccan government, with tacit support from France and the United States, and the remainder by the SADR, backed by Algeria.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">
        <a href="#cite_note-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Internationally, countries such as
       <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">
        Russia
       </a>
       have taken a generally ambiguous and neutral position on each side's claims, and have pressed both parties to agree on a peaceful resolution. Both Morocco and Polisario have sought to boost their claims by accumulating formal recognition, essentially from African, Asian, and Latin American states in the developing world. The Polisario Front has won formal recognition for SADR from
       <a href="/wiki/Political_status_of_Western_Sahara#States_supporting_Sahrawi_claims_on_Western_Sahara" title="Political status of Western Sahara">
        37 states
       </a>
       , and was extended membership in the
       <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">
        African Union
       </a>
       . Morocco has won support for its position from several African governments and from most of the
       <a href="/wiki/Muslim_world" title="Muslim world">
        Muslim world
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Arab_League" title="Arab League">
        Arab League
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
        <a href="#cite_note-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In both instances, recognitions have, over the past two decades, been extended and withdrawn according to changing international trends.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2011)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       As of 2017
       <sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Western_Sahara&amp;action=edit">
         [update]
        </a>
       </sup>
       , no other
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Member_state_of_the_United_Nations" title="Member state of the United Nations">
        member state of the United Nations
       </a>
       has ever officially recognized Moroccan
       <a href="/wiki/Sovereignty" title="Sovereignty">
        sovereignty
       </a>
       over parts of Western Sahara.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
        <a href="#cite_note-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
        <a href="#cite_note-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
        <a href="#cite_note-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
       However, a
       <a href="/wiki/Political_status_of_Western_Sahara#States_supporting_Moroccan_claims_on_Western_Sahara" title="Political status of Western Sahara">
        number of countries have expressed their support
       </a>
       for a future recognition of the Moroccan annexation of the territory
       <a href="/wiki/Western_Sahara_Autonomy_Proposal" title="Western Sahara Autonomy Proposal">
        as an autonomous part of the Kingdom
       </a>
       . Overall, the annexation has not garnered as much attention in the
       <a href="/wiki/International_community" title="International community">
        international community
       </a>
       as many other disputed annexations (e.g.
       <a href="/wiki/Annexation_of_Crimea_by_the_Russian_Federation" title="Annexation of Crimea by the Russian Federation">
        the Russian annexation of Crimea
       </a>
       ).
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">
        Geography
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Western_Sahara" title="Geography of Western Sahara">
        Geography of Western Sahara
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Western Sahara is located in Northern Africa, bordering the North Atlantic Ocean, between Mauritania and Morocco. It also borders Algeria to the northeast.
      </p>
      <p>
       The land is some of the most arid and inhospitable on the planet. The land along the coast is low flat desert and rises, especially in the north, to small mountains reaching up to 600 metres (2,000 ft) on the eastern side.
      </p>
      <p>
       While the area can experience flash flooding in the spring, there are no permanent streams. At times a cool off-shore current can produce fog and heavy dew. The interior experiences extreme summer heat with averages highs reaching as high as 43–45 °C (109–113 °F) in July and in August ; during "winter", days are still hot to very hot with averages highs from 25 to 30 °C (77 to 86 °F) but in the northern part of the territory, the thermometer may drop below 0 °C (32 °F) at night and it can be freezing outside in December and in January although it's an exceedingly rare event.
      </p>
      <ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional left">
       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px">
        <div style="width: 155px">
         <div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;">
          <div style="margin:15px auto;">
           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Western_Sahara_(orthographic_projection).svg">
            <img alt="" data-file-height="550" data-file-width="550" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Western_Sahara_%28orthographic_projection%29.svg/120px-Western_Sahara_%28orthographic_projection%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Western_Sahara_%28orthographic_projection%29.svg/180px-Western_Sahara_%28orthographic_projection%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Western_Sahara_%28orthographic_projection%29.svg/240px-Western_Sahara_%28orthographic_projection%29.svg.png 2x" width="120"/>
           </a>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="gallerytext">
          <p>
           Western Sahara in Africa.
          </p>
         </div>
        </div>
       </li>
       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px">
        <div style="width: 155px">
         <div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;">
          <div style="margin:21px auto;">
           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Western_Sahara_Topography.png">
            <img alt="" data-file-height="1183" data-file-width="1318" height="108" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Western_Sahara_Topography.png/120px-Western_Sahara_Topography.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Western_Sahara_Topography.png/180px-Western_Sahara_Topography.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Western_Sahara_Topography.png/240px-Western_Sahara_Topography.png 2x" width="120"/>
           </a>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="gallerytext">
          <p>
           Topography of Western Sahara.
          </p>
         </div>
        </div>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">
        History
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Western_Sahara" title="History of Western Sahara">
        History of Western Sahara
       </a>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Early_history">
        Early history
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Further information:
       <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Serer_history" title="Timeline of Serer history">
        Timeline of Serer history
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Serer_history" title="Serer history">
        Serer history
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The earliest known inhabitants of Western Sahara were the
       <a href="/wiki/Gaetuli" title="Gaetuli">
        Gaetuli
       </a>
       . Depending on the century, Roman-era sources describe the area as inhabited by Gaetulian Autololes or the Gaetulian Daradae tribes. Berber heritage is still evident from regional and place-name
       <a href="/wiki/Toponymy" title="Toponymy">
        toponymy
       </a>
       , as well as from tribal names.
      </p>
      <p>
       Other early inhabitants of Western Sahara may be the
       <a href="/wiki/Bafour" title="Bafour">
        Bafour
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
        <a href="#cite_note-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and later the
       <a href="/wiki/Serer_people" title="Serer people">
        Serer
       </a>
       . The Bafour were later replaced or absorbed by
       <a href="/wiki/Berber_languages" title="Berber languages">
        Berber-speaking
       </a>
       populations which eventually merged in turn with the migrating
       <a href="/wiki/Beni_%E1%B8%A4ass%C4%81n" title="Beni Ḥassān">
        Beni Ḥassān
       </a>
       Arab tribes.
      </p>
      <p>
       The arrival of Islam in the 8th century played a major role in the development of the
       <a href="/wiki/Maghreb" title="Maghreb">
        Maghreb
       </a>
       region. Trade developed further, and the territory may have been one of the routes for
       <a href="/wiki/Camel_train" title="Camel train">
        caravans
       </a>
       , especially between
       <a href="/wiki/Marrakesh" title="Marrakesh">
        Marrakesh
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Tombouctou_Region" title="Tombouctou Region">
        Tombouctou
       </a>
       in Mali.
      </p>
      <p>
       In the 11th century, the
       <a href="/wiki/Maqil" title="Maqil">
        Maqil
       </a>
       Arabs (fewer than 200 individuals) settled in
       <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">
        Morocco
       </a>
       (mainly in the
       <a href="/wiki/Draa_River" title="Draa River">
        Draa River
       </a>
       valley, between the
       <a href="/wiki/Moulouya_River" title="Moulouya River">
        Moulouya River
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Tafilalt" title="Tafilalt">
        Tafilalt
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Taourirt,_Morocco" title="Taourirt, Morocco">
        Taourirt
       </a>
       ).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-khaldun_15-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-khaldun-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Towards the end of the
       <a href="/wiki/Almohad_Caliphate" title="Almohad Caliphate">
        Almohad Caliphate
       </a>
       , the Beni Hassan, a sub-tribe of the Maqil, were called by the local ruler of the
       <a href="/wiki/Sous" title="Sous">
        Sous
       </a>
       to quell a rebellion; they settled in the Sous
       <a href="/wiki/Ksar" title="Ksar">
        Ksours
       </a>
       and controlled such cities as
       <a href="/wiki/Taroudant" title="Taroudant">
        Taroudant
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-khaldun_15-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-khaldun-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       During
       <a href="/wiki/Marinid_dynasty" title="Marinid dynasty">
        Marinid dynasty
       </a>
       rule, the Beni Hassan rebelled but were defeated by the Sultan and escaped beyond the Saguia el-Hamra dry river.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-khaldun_15-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-khaldun-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
        <a href="#cite_note-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Beni Hassan then were at constant war with the
       <a href="/wiki/Lamtuna" title="Lamtuna">
        Lamtuna
       </a>
       nomadic Berbers of the
       <a href="/wiki/Sahara" title="Sahara">
        Sahara
       </a>
       . Over roughly five centuries, through a complex process of acculturation and mixing seen elsewhere in the Maghreb and North Africa, some of the indigenous Berber tribes mixed with the Maqil Arab tribes and formed a culture unique to Morocco and Mauritania.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2011)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Spanish_province">
        Spanish province
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Sahara" title="Spanish Sahara">
        Spanish Sahara
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spanish_Morocco" title="Spanish Morocco">
        Spanish Morocco
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Western_Sahara_1876.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="641" data-file-width="746" height="344" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Western_Sahara_1876.png/400px-Western_Sahara_1876.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Western_Sahara_1876.png/600px-Western_Sahara_1876.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/4f/Western_Sahara_1876.png 2x" width="400"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Western_Sahara_1876.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Western Sahara 1876
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       While initial Spanish interest in the Sahara was focused on using it as a port for the slave trade, by the 1700s Spain had transitioned economic activity on the Saharan coast towards commercial fishing.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
        <a href="#cite_note-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
       After an agreement among the European colonial powers at the
       <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Conference" title="Berlin Conference">
        Berlin Conference
       </a>
       in 1884 on the division of
       <a href="/wiki/Scramble_for_Africa" title="Scramble for Africa">
        spheres of influence in Africa
       </a>
       , Spain seized control of Western Sahara and established it as a Spanish colony.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
        <a href="#cite_note-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
       After 1939 and the outbreak of World War II, this area was administered by
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spanish_Morocco" title="Spanish Morocco">
        Spanish Morocco
       </a>
       . As a consequence,
       <a href="/wiki/Ahmed_Belbachir_Haskouri" title="Ahmed Belbachir Haskouri">
        Ahmed Belbachir Haskouri
       </a>
       , the Chief of Cabinet, General Secretary of the Government of Spanish Morocco, cooperated with the Spanish to select governors in that area. The Saharan lords who were already in prominent positions, such as the members of Maa El Ainain family, provided a recommended list of candidates for new governors. Together with the Spanish High Commissioner, Belbachir selected from this list.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2010)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       During the annual celebration of
       <a href="/wiki/Muhammad" title="Muhammad">
        Muhammad
       </a>
       's birthday, these lords paid their respects to the caliph to show loyalty to the Moroccan monarchy.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2010)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Morocco_Protectorate.svg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="388" data-file-width="406" height="210" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Morocco_Protectorate.svg/220px-Morocco_Protectorate.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Morocco_Protectorate.svg/330px-Morocco_Protectorate.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Morocco_Protectorate.svg/440px-Morocco_Protectorate.svg.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Morocco_Protectorate.svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Spanish and French protectorates in Morocco and Spanish Sahara, 1912.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       As time went by, Spanish colonial rule began to unravel with the general wave of decolonization after World War II; former North African and sub-Saharan African possessions and protectorates gained independence from European powers. Spanish decolonization proceeded more slowly, but internal political and social pressures for it in mainland Spain built up towards the end of
       <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Franco" title="Francisco Franco">
        Francisco Franco
       </a>
       's rule. There was a global trend towards complete
       <a href="/wiki/Decolonization" title="Decolonization">
        decolonization
       </a>
       . Spain began rapidly to divest itself of most of its remaining colonial possessions. By 1974–75 the government issued promises of a referendum on independence in Western Sahara.
      </p>
      <p>
       At the same time, Morocco and Mauritania, which had historical and competing claims of sovereignty over the territory, argued that it had been artificially separated from their territories by the European colonial powers. Algeria, which also bordered the territory, viewed their demands with suspicion, as Morocco also claimed the Algerian provinces of
       <a href="/wiki/Tindouf_Province" title="Tindouf Province">
        Tindouf
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/B%C3%A9char_Province" title="Béchar Province">
        Béchar
       </a>
       . After arguing for a process of decolonization to be guided by the United Nations, the Algerian government under
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Houari_Boum%C3%A9di%C3%A8nne" title="Houari Boumédiènne">
        Houari Boumédiènne
       </a>
       in 1975 committed to assisting the Polisario Front, which opposed both Moroccan and Mauritanian claims and demanded full independence of Western Sahara.
      </p>
      <p>
       The UN attempted to settle these disputes through a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UN_visiting_mission_to_Spanish_Sahara" title="UN visiting mission to Spanish Sahara">
        visiting mission
       </a>
       in late 1975, as well as a
       <a href="/wiki/International_Court_of_Justice_Advisory_Opinion_on_Western_Sahara" title="International Court of Justice Advisory Opinion on Western Sahara">
        verdict
       </a>
       from the
       <a href="/wiki/International_Court_of_Justice" title="International Court of Justice">
        International Court of Justice
       </a>
       (ICJ). It acknowledged that Western Sahara had historical links with Morocco and Mauritania, but not sufficient to prove the sovereignty of either State over the territory at the time of the Spanish colonisation. The population of the territory thus possessed the right of
       <a href="/wiki/Self-determination" title="Self-determination">
        self-determination
       </a>
       . On 6 November 1975 Morocco initiated the
       <a href="/wiki/Green_March" title="Green March">
        Green March
       </a>
       into Western Sahara; 350,000 unarmed Moroccans converged on the city of
       <a href="/wiki/Tarfaya" title="Tarfaya">
        Tarfaya
       </a>
       in southern Morocco and waited for a signal from King
       <a href="/wiki/Hassan_II_of_Morocco" title="Hassan II of Morocco">
        Hassan II of Morocco
       </a>
       to cross the border in a peaceful march. A few days before, on 31 October, Moroccan troops invaded Western Sahara from the north.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
        <a href="#cite_note-19">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Demands_for_independence">
        Demands for independence
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Western_sahara_walls_moroccan_map-en.svg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1302" data-file-width="1676" height="272" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Western_sahara_walls_moroccan_map-en.svg/350px-Western_sahara_walls_moroccan_map-en.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Western_sahara_walls_moroccan_map-en.svg/525px-Western_sahara_walls_moroccan_map-en.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Western_sahara_walls_moroccan_map-en.svg/700px-Western_sahara_walls_moroccan_map-en.svg.png 2x" width="350"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Western_sahara_walls_moroccan_map-en.svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         System of the
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moroccan_Wall" title="Moroccan Wall">
          Moroccan Walls
         </a>
         in Western Sahara set up in the 1980s
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:RASD_-_Commemoration_of_the_30th_independence_day_in_the_Liberated_Territories_(2006).jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/RASD_-_Commemoration_of_the_30th_independence_day_in_the_Liberated_Territories_%282006%29.jpg/220px-RASD_-_Commemoration_of_the_30th_independence_day_in_the_Liberated_Territories_%282006%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/RASD_-_Commemoration_of_the_30th_independence_day_in_the_Liberated_Territories_%282006%29.jpg/330px-RASD_-_Commemoration_of_the_30th_independence_day_in_the_Liberated_Territories_%282006%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/RASD_-_Commemoration_of_the_30th_independence_day_in_the_Liberated_Territories_%282006%29.jpg/440px-RASD_-_Commemoration_of_the_30th_independence_day_in_the_Liberated_Territories_%282006%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:RASD_-_Commemoration_of_the_30th_independence_day_in_the_Liberated_Territories_(2006).jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Commemoration of the 30th independence day from
         <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">
          Spain
         </a>
         in the
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Free_Zone_(Western_Sahara)" title="Free Zone (Western Sahara)">
          Liberated Territories
         </a>
         (2005)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In the waning days of General
       <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Franco" title="Francisco Franco">
        Franco
       </a>
       's rule, and after the
       <a href="/wiki/Green_March" title="Green March">
        Green March
       </a>
       , the Spanish government signed a
       <a href="/wiki/Madrid_Accords" title="Madrid Accords">
        tripartite agreement
       </a>
       with Morocco and Mauritania as it moved to transfer the territory on 14 November 1975. The accords were based on a bipartite administration, and Morocco and Mauritania each moved to annex the territories, with Morocco taking control of the northern two-thirds of Western Sahara as its
       <a href="/wiki/Southern_Provinces" title="Southern Provinces">
        Southern Provinces
       </a>
       , and Mauritania taking control of the southern third as
       <a href="/wiki/Tiris_al-Gharbiyya" title="Tiris al-Gharbiyya">
        Tiris al-Gharbiyya
       </a>
       . Spain terminated its presence in Spanish Sahara within three months, repatriating Spanish remains from its cemeteries.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
        <a href="#cite_note-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The Moroccan and Mauritanian annexations were resisted by the
       <a href="/wiki/Polisario_Front" title="Polisario Front">
        Polisario Front
       </a>
       , which had gained backing from
       <a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">
        Algeria
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
        <a href="#cite_note-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It initiated guerrilla warfare and, in 1979, Mauritania withdrew due to pressure from Polisario, including a bombardment of its capital and other economic targets. Morocco extended its control to the rest of the territory. It gradually contained the guerrillas by setting up
       <a href="/wiki/Moroccan_Western_Sahara_Wall" title="Moroccan Western Sahara Wall">
        the extensive sand-berm in the desert
       </a>
       (known as the Border Wall or Moroccan Wall) to exclude guerrilla fighters.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
        <a href="#cite_note-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Hostilities ceased in a 1991 cease-fire, overseen by the peacekeeping mission
       <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Mission_for_the_Referendum_in_Western_Sahara" title="United Nations Mission for the Referendum in Western Sahara">
        MINURSO
       </a>
       , under the terms of a UN
       <a href="/wiki/Settlement_Plan" title="Settlement Plan">
        Settlement Plan
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Stalling_of_the_referendum_and_Settlement_Plan">
        Stalling of the referendum and Settlement Plan
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:752px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Maps_of_Western_Sahara.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="433" data-file-width="1472" height="221" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Maps_of_Western_Sahara.png/750px-Maps_of_Western_Sahara.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Maps_of_Western_Sahara.png/1125px-Maps_of_Western_Sahara.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/de/Maps_of_Western_Sahara.png 2x" width="750"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Maps_of_Western_Sahara.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <div class="center" style="width:auto; margin-left:auto; margin-right:auto;">
          Ways to show Western Sahara in maps
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The referendum, originally scheduled for 1992, foresaw giving the local population the option between independence or affirming integration with Morocco, but it quickly stalled. In 1997, the
       <a href="/wiki/Houston_Agreement" title="Houston Agreement">
        Houston Agreement
       </a>
       attempted to revive the proposal for a referendum but likewise has hitherto not had success. As of 2010
       <sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Western_Sahara&amp;action=edit">
         [update]
        </a>
       </sup>
       , negotiations over terms have not resulted in any substantive action. At the heart of the dispute lies the question of who qualifies to be registered to participate in the referendum, and, since about the year 2000, Morocco considers that since there is no agreement on persons entitled to vote, a referendum is not possible. Meanwhile, Polisario still insisted on a referendum with independence as a clear option, without offering a solution to the problem of who is qualified to be registered to participate in it.
      </p>
      <p>
       Both sides blame each other for the stalling of the referendum. The Polisario has insisted on only allowing those found on the 1974 Spanish Census lists (see below) to vote, while Morocco has insisted that the census was flawed by evasion and sought the inclusion of members of Sahrawi tribes which escaped from Spanish invasion to the north of Morocco by the 19th century.
      </p>
      <p>
       Efforts by the UN special envoys to find a common ground for both parties did not succeed. By 1999 the UN had identified about 85,000 voters, with nearly half of them in the Moroccan-controlled parts of Western Sahara or Southern Morocco, and the others scattered between the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sahrawi_refugee_camps_in_Tindouf_Province,_Algeria" title="Sahrawi refugee camps in Tindouf Province, Algeria">
        Tindouf refugee camps
       </a>
       , Mauritania and other places of exile. Polisario accepted this voter list, as it had done with the previous list presented by the UN (both of them originally based on the Spanish census of 1974), but Morocco refused and, as rejected voter candidates began a mass-appeals procedure, insisted that each application be scrutinized individually. This again brought the process to a halt.
      </p>
      <p>
       According to a NATO delegation, MINURSO election observers stated in 1999, as the deadlock continued, that "if the number of voters does not rise significantly the odds were slightly on the
       <a href="/wiki/Sahrawi_Arab_Democratic_Republic" title="Sahrawi Arab Democratic Republic">
        SADR
       </a>
       side".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
        <a href="#cite_note-23">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
       By 2001, the process had effectively stalemated and the UN Secretary-General asked the parties for the first time to explore other, third-way solutions. Indeed, shortly after the Houston Agreement (1997), Morocco officially declared that it was "no longer necessary" to include an option of independence on the ballot, offering instead autonomy. Erik Jensen, who played an administrative role in MINURSO, wrote that neither side would agree to a voter registration in which they were destined to lose (see
       <i>
        <a href="#Further_reading">
         Western Sahara: Anatomy of a Stalemate
        </a>
       </i>
       ).
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Baker_Plan">
        Baker Plan
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Baker_Plan" title="Baker Plan">
        Baker Plan
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       As personal envoy of the Secretary-General,
       <a href="/wiki/James_Baker" title="James Baker">
        James Baker
       </a>
       visited all sides and produced the document known as the "Baker Plan".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UN_S2000461_24-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-UN_S2000461-24">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This was discussed by the
       <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">
        United Nations Security Council
       </a>
       in 2000, and envisioned an autonomous
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Western_Sahara_Authority" title="Western Sahara Authority">
        Western Sahara Authority
       </a>
       (WSA), which would be followed after five years by the referendum. Every person present in the territory would be allowed to vote, regardless of birthplace and with no regard to the Spanish census. It was rejected by both sides, although it was initially derived from a Moroccan proposal. According to Baker's draft, tens of thousands of post-annexation immigrants from Morocco proper (viewed by Polisario as settlers but by Morocco as legitimate inhabitants of the area) would be granted the vote in the Sahrawi independence referendum, and the ballot would be split three ways by the inclusion of an unspecified "
       <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_administrative_division" title="Autonomous administrative division">
        autonomy
       </a>
       ", further undermining the independence camp. Morocco was also allowed to keep its army in the area and retain control over all security issues during both the autonomy years and the election. In 2002, the Moroccan king stated that the referendum idea was "out of date" since it "cannot be implemented";
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
        <a href="#cite_note-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Polisario retorted that that was only because of the King's refusal to allow it to take place.
      </p>
      <p>
       In 2003, a new version of the plan was made official, with some additions spelling out the powers of the WSA, making it less reliant on Moroccan
       <a href="/wiki/Devolution" title="Devolution">
        devolution
       </a>
       . It also provided further detail on the referendum process in order to make it harder to stall or subvert. This second draft, commonly known as Baker II, was accepted by the Polisario as a "basis of negotiations" to the surprise of many.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
        <a href="#cite_note-26">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This appeared to abandon Polisario's previous position of only negotiating based on the standards of voter identification from 1991 (i.e. the Spanish census). After that, the draft quickly garnered widespread international support, culminating in the UN Security Council's unanimous endorsement of the plan in the summer of 2003.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="End_of_the_2000s">
        End of the 2000s
       </span>
      </h3>
      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Update" role="presentation">
       <tr>
        <td class="mbox-image">
         <div style="width:52px">
          <img alt="Ambox current red.svg" data-file-height="290" data-file-width="360" height="34" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/42px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/63px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/84px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 2x" width="42"/>
         </div>
        </td>
        <td class="mbox-text">
         <div class="mbox-text-span">
          Parts of this article (those related to the
          <a href="/wiki/Manhasset_negotiations" title="Manhasset negotiations">
           Manhasset negotiations
          </a>
          (not in article)) need to be
          <b>
           updated
          </b>
          .
          <span class="hide-when-compact">
           Please update this article to reflect recent events or newly available information.
          </span>
          <small>
           <i>
            (September 2013)
           </i>
          </small>
         </div>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Western_sahara_landscape_(north).jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="315" data-file-width="800" height="118" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Western_sahara_landscape_%28north%29.jpg/300px-Western_sahara_landscape_%28north%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Western_sahara_landscape_%28north%29.jpg/450px-Western_sahara_landscape_%28north%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Western_sahara_landscape_%28north%29.jpg/600px-Western_sahara_landscape_%28north%29.jpg 2x" width="300"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Western_sahara_landscape_(north).jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         North Western Sahara landscape.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Baker resigned his post at the United Nations in 2004; his term did not see the crisis resolved.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">
        <a href="#cite_note-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
       His resignation followed several months of failed attempts to get Morocco to enter into formal negotiations on the plan, but he met with rejection. The new king,
       <a href="/wiki/Mohammed_VI_of_Morocco" title="Mohammed VI of Morocco">
        Mohammed VI of Morocco
       </a>
       , opposes any referendum on independence, and has said Morocco will never agree to one: "We shall not give up one inch of our beloved Sahara, not a grain of its sand."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
        <a href="#cite_note-28">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Instead, he proposes, through an appointed advisory body
       <a href="/wiki/Royal_Advisory_Council_for_Saharan_Affairs" title="Royal Advisory Council for Saharan Affairs">
        Royal Advisory Council for Saharan Affairs
       </a>
       (CORCAS), a self-governing Western Sahara as an autonomous community within Morocco. His father,
       <a href="/wiki/Hassan_II_of_Morocco" title="Hassan II of Morocco">
        Hassan II of Morocco
       </a>
       , initially supported the referendum idea in principle in 1982, and in signed contracts with Polisario and the UN in 1991 and 1997. No major powers have expressed interest in forcing the issue, however, and Morocco has shown little interest in a real referendum.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Saara-Ocidental-Baia-Dakhla-Luis-Filipe-Gaspar.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="653" data-file-width="980" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Saara-Ocidental-Baia-Dakhla-Luis-Filipe-Gaspar.jpg/220px-Saara-Ocidental-Baia-Dakhla-Luis-Filipe-Gaspar.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Saara-Ocidental-Baia-Dakhla-Luis-Filipe-Gaspar.jpg/330px-Saara-Ocidental-Baia-Dakhla-Luis-Filipe-Gaspar.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Saara-Ocidental-Baia-Dakhla-Luis-Filipe-Gaspar.jpg/440px-Saara-Ocidental-Baia-Dakhla-Luis-Filipe-Gaspar.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Saara-Ocidental-Baia-Dakhla-Luis-Filipe-Gaspar.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Dakhla Bay, near
         <a href="/wiki/Dakhla,_Western_Sahara" title="Dakhla, Western Sahara">
          Dakhla
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The UN has put forth no replacement strategy after the breakdown of Baker II, and renewed fighting has been raised as a possibility. In 2005, former United Nations Secretary-General
       <a href="/wiki/Kofi_Annan" title="Kofi Annan">
        Kofi Annan
       </a>
       reported increased military activity on both sides of the front and breaches of several cease-fire provisions against strengthening military fortifications.
      </p>
      <p>
       Morocco has repeatedly tried to get Algeria into bilateral negotiations, based on its view of Polisario as the
       <a href="/wiki/The_Monkey_and_the_Cat" title="The Monkey and the Cat">
        cat's paw
       </a>
       of the Algerian military. It has received vocal support from France and occasionally (and currently) from the United States. These negotiations would define the exact limits of a Western Sahara autonomy under Moroccan rule but only after Morocco's "inalienable right" to the territory was recognized as a precondition to the talks. The Algerian government has consistently refused, claiming it has neither the will nor the right to negotiate on the behalf of the Polisario Front.
      </p>
      <p>
       Demonstrations and riots by supporters of independence or a referendum broke out in the Moroccan-controlled parts of Western Sahara in May 2005 and in parts of southern Morocco (notably the town of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Assa_(Morocco)" title="Assa (Morocco)">
        Assa
       </a>
       ). They were met by police. Several international human rights organizations expressed concern at what they termed abuse by Moroccan security forces, and a number of Sahrawi activists have been jailed. Pro-independence Sahrawi sources, including the Polisario, have given these demonstrations the name "
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Independence_Intifada_(Western_Sahara)" title="Independence Intifada (Western Sahara)">
        Independence Intifada
       </a>
       ", while most sources have tended to see the events as being of limited importance. International press and other media coverage has been sparse, and reporting is complicated by the Moroccan government's policy of strictly controlling independent media coverage within the territory.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:289px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Manifestation_in_Madrid_for_the_independence_of_the_Western_Sahara_(11).jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2048" data-file-width="3072" height="191" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Manifestation_in_Madrid_for_the_independence_of_the_Western_Sahara_%2811%29.jpg/287px-Manifestation_in_Madrid_for_the_independence_of_the_Western_Sahara_%2811%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Manifestation_in_Madrid_for_the_independence_of_the_Western_Sahara_%2811%29.jpg/431px-Manifestation_in_Madrid_for_the_independence_of_the_Western_Sahara_%2811%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Manifestation_in_Madrid_for_the_independence_of_the_Western_Sahara_%2811%29.jpg/574px-Manifestation_in_Madrid_for_the_independence_of_the_Western_Sahara_%2811%29.jpg 2x" width="287"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Manifestation_in_Madrid_for_the_independence_of_the_Western_Sahara_(11).jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A demonstration in Madrid for the independence of Western Sahara.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Demonstrations and protests still occur, even after Morocco declared in February 2006 that it was contemplating a plan for devolving a limited variant of autonomy to the territory but still explicitly refused any referendum on independence. As of January 2007, the plan had not been made public, though the Moroccan government claimed that it was more or less complete.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
        <a href="#cite_note-29">
         [29]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Polisario has intermittently threatened to resume fighting, referring to the Moroccan refusal of a referendum as a breach of the
       <a href="/wiki/Settlement_Plan" title="Settlement Plan">
        cease-fire terms
       </a>
       , but most observers seem to consider armed conflict unlikely without the green light from
       <a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">
        Algeria
       </a>
       , which houses the Sahrawis' refugee camps and has been the main military sponsor of the movement.
      </p>
      <p>
       In April 2007, the government of Morocco suggested that a self-governing entity, through the
       <a href="/wiki/Royal_Advisory_Council_for_Saharan_Affairs" title="Royal Advisory Council for Saharan Affairs">
        Royal Advisory Council for Saharan Affairs
       </a>
       (CORCAS), should govern the territory with some degree of autonomy for Western Sahara. The project was presented to the UN Security Council in mid-April 2007. The stalemating of the Moroccan proposal options has led the UN in the recent "Report of the UN Secretary-General" to ask the parties to enter into direct and unconditional negotiations to reach a mutually accepted political solution.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
        <a href="#cite_note-30">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="The_2010s">
        The 2010s
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       In October 2010 Gadaym Izik camp was set up near
       <a href="/wiki/Laayoune" title="Laayoune">
        Laayoune
       </a>
       as a protest by displaced
       <a href="/wiki/Sahrawi_people" title="Sahrawi people">
        Sahrawi people
       </a>
       about their living conditions. It was home to more than 12,000 people. In November 2010 Moroccan security forces entered Gadaym Izik camp in the early hours of the morning, using helicopters and water cannon to force people to leave. The Polisario Front said Moroccan security forces had killed a 26-year-old protester at the camp, a claim denied by Morocco. Protesters in Laayoune threw stones at police and set fire to tires and vehicles. Several buildings, including a TV station, were also set on fire. Moroccan officials said five security personnel had been killed in the unrest.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
        <a href="#cite_note-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       On 15 November 2010, the Moroccan government accused the Algerian secret services of orchestrating and financing the Gadaym Izik camp with the intent to destabilize the region. The Spanish press was accused of mounting a campaign of disinformation to support the Saharwi initiative, and all foreign reporters were either prevented from travelling or else expelled from the area.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
        <a href="#cite_note-32">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The protest coincided with a fresh round of negotiations at the UN.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
        <a href="#cite_note-33">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 2016, the European Union (EU) declared that "Western Sahara is not part of Moroccan territory."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
        <a href="#cite_note-34">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In March 2016, Morocco "expelled more than 70 U.N. civilian staffers with MINURSO" due to strained relations after
       <a href="/wiki/Ban_Ki-moon" title="Ban Ki-moon">
        Ban Ki-moon
       </a>
       called Morocco's annexation of Western Sahara an "occupation".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">
        <a href="#cite_note-35">
         [35]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">
        Politics
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Western_Sahara" title="Politics of Western Sahara">
        Politics of Western Sahara
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Morocco" title="Foreign relations of Morocco">
        Foreign relations of Morocco
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_the_Sahrawi_Arab_Democratic_Republic" title="Foreign relations of the Sahrawi Arab Democratic Republic">
        Foreign relations of the Sahrawi Arab Democratic Republic
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Laayoune-miltary_checkpoint.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="523" data-file-width="800" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Laayoune-miltary_checkpoint.jpg/220px-Laayoune-miltary_checkpoint.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Laayoune-miltary_checkpoint.jpg/330px-Laayoune-miltary_checkpoint.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Laayoune-miltary_checkpoint.jpg/440px-Laayoune-miltary_checkpoint.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Laayoune-miltary_checkpoint.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A police checkpoint in the suburbs of
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/El_Aai%C3%BAn" title="El Aaiún">
          Laayoune
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Sovereignty" title="Sovereignty">
        Sovereignty
       </a>
       over Western Sahara is contested between
       <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">
        Morocco
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Polisario_Front" title="Polisario Front">
        Polisario Front
       </a>
       and its legal status remains unresolved. The United Nations considers it to be a "
       <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_list_of_Non-Self-Governing_Territories" title="United Nations list of Non-Self-Governing Territories">
        Non-Self-Governing Territory
       </a>
       ".
      </p>
      <p>
       Formally, Morocco is administered by a
       <a href="/wiki/Bicameralism" title="Bicameralism">
        bicameral
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Morocco" title="Parliament of Morocco">
        parliament
       </a>
       under a
       <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">
        constitutional monarchy
       </a>
       . The last elections to
       <a href="/wiki/House_of_Representatives_(Morocco)" title="House of Representatives (Morocco)">
        the parliament's lower house
       </a>
       were deemed reasonably free and fair by international observers.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2011)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       Certain powers, such as the capacity to appoint the government and to dissolve parliament, remain in the hands of
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_rulers_of_Morocco" title="List of rulers of Morocco">
        the monarch
       </a>
       . The Morocco-controlled parts of Western Sahara are divided into
       <a href="/wiki/Southern_Provinces" title="Southern Provinces">
        several provinces
       </a>
       that are treated as integral parts of the kingdom. The Moroccan government heavily subsidizes the Saharan provinces under its control with cut-rate fuel and related subsidies, to appease nationalist dissent and attract immigrants from Sahrawis and other communities in Morocco proper.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Thobhani_36-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Thobhani-36">
         [36]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Government_in_exile" title="Government in exile">
        exiled government
       </a>
       of the self-proclaimed
       <a href="/wiki/Sahrawi_Arab_Democratic_Republic" title="Sahrawi Arab Democratic Republic">
        Sahrawi Arab Democratic Republic
       </a>
       (SADR) is a form of single-party parliamentary and presidential system, but according to its constitution, this will be changed into a multi-party system at the achievement of independence. It is presently based at the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sahrawi_refugee_camps_in_Tindouf_Province,_Algeria" title="Sahrawi refugee camps in Tindouf Province, Algeria">
        Tindouf refugee camps
       </a>
       in Algeria, which it controls. It also controls the part of Western Sahara to the east of the Moroccan Wall, known as the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Free_Zone_(region)" title="Free Zone (region)">
         liberated territories
        </a>
       </i>
       . This area has a very small population, estimated to be approximately 30,000 nomads.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nrc.no_37-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-nrc.no-37">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Moroccan government views it as a no-man's land patrolled by UN troops. The SADR government whose troops also patrol the area have proclaimed a village in the area,
       <a href="/wiki/Bir_Lehlou" title="Bir Lehlou">
        Bir Lehlou
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Tifariti" title="Tifariti">
        Tifariti
       </a>
       , as SADR's former and actual temporary factual capitals.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights">
        Human rights
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Western_Sahara" title="Human rights in Western Sahara">
        Human rights in Western Sahara
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sangar_western_sahara.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="414" data-file-width="597" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Sangar_western_sahara.jpg/220px-Sangar_western_sahara.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Sangar_western_sahara.jpg/330px-Sangar_western_sahara.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Sangar_western_sahara.jpg/440px-Sangar_western_sahara.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sangar_western_sahara.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A
         <a href="/wiki/Sangar_(fortification)" title="Sangar (fortification)">
          sangar
         </a>
         (fortification) from the Western Sahara conflict. The fortification is built of rocks on top of a mesa overlooking the Grart Chwchia, Al Gada, Western Sahara. The Sangar is facing north and was probably built by the Sahrawis in the 1980s.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tamekinprison.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="320" height="330" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Tamekinprison.jpg/220px-Tamekinprison.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/05/Tamekinprison.jpg 1.5x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tamekinprison.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Sahrawi_people" title="Sahrawi people">
          Sahrawi
         </a>
         human-rights defender
         <a href="/wiki/Ali_Salem_Tamek" title="Ali Salem Tamek">
          Ali Salem Tamek
         </a>
         in
         <a href="/wiki/Ait_Meloul_Prison" title="Ait Meloul Prison">
          Ait Meloul Prison
         </a>
         , Morocco
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
          <a href="#cite_note-38">
           [38]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Western Sahara conflict has resulted in severe human-rights abuses, constantly reported by external reporters and HR activists,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">
        <a href="#cite_note-39">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
       most notably the displacement of tens of thousands of Sahrawi civilians from the country, the expulsion of tens of thousands of Moroccan civilians by the Algerian government from Algeria,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">
        <a href="#cite_note-40">
         [40]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and numerous casualties of war and repression.
      </p>
      <p>
       During the war years (1975–91), both sides accused each other of targeting civilians. Moroccan claims of Polisario terrorism has generally little to no support abroad, with the US, EU,
       <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">
        AU
       </a>
       and UN all refusing to include the group on their
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._State_Department_list_of_Foreign_Terrorist_Organizations" title="U.S. State Department list of Foreign Terrorist Organizations">
        lists
       </a>
       of terrorist organizations. Polisario leaders maintain that they are ideologically opposed to terrorism, and insist that collective punishment and
       <a href="/wiki/Forced_disappearance" title="Forced disappearance">
        forced disappearances
       </a>
       among Sahrawi civilians
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">
        <a href="#cite_note-41">
         [41]
        </a>
       </sup>
       should be considered
       <a href="/wiki/State_terrorism" title="State terrorism">
        state terrorism
       </a>
       on the part of Morocco.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">
        <a href="#cite_note-42">
         [42]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Both Morocco and the Polisario additionally accuse each other of violating the human rights of the populations under their control, in the
       <a href="/wiki/Southern_Provinces" title="Southern Provinces">
        Moroccan-controlled parts of Western Sahara
       </a>
       and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sahrawi_refugee_camps_in_Tindouf_Province,_Algeria" title="Sahrawi refugee camps in Tindouf Province, Algeria">
        Tindouf refugee camps
       </a>
       in Algeria, respectively. Morocco and organizations such as
       <a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/France_Libert%C3%A9s_-_Fondation_Danielle-Mitterrand" title="fr:France Libertés - Fondation Danielle-Mitterrand">
        France Libertés
       </a>
       consider Algeria to be directly responsible for any crimes committed on its territory, and accuse the country of having been directly involved in such violations.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tindouf1_43-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Tindouf1-43">
         [43]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">
        Morocco
       </a>
       has been repeatedly criticized for its actions in Western Sahara by international human rights organizations including:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Amnesty_International" title="Amnesty International">
         Amnesty International
        </a>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">
         <a href="#cite_note-44">
          [44]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">
         Human Rights Watch
        </a>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">
         <a href="#cite_note-45">
          [45]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">
         <a href="#cite_note-46">
          [46]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_Organization_Against_Torture" title="World Organization Against Torture">
         World Organization Against Torture
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Freedom_House" title="Freedom House">
         Freedom House
        </a>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">
         <a href="#cite_note-47">
          [47]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Reporters_Without_Borders" title="Reporters Without Borders">
         Reporters Without Borders
        </a>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">
         <a href="#cite_note-48">
          [48]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/International_Committee_of_the_Red_Cross" title="International Committee of the Red Cross">
         International Committee of the Red Cross
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/OHCHR" title="OHCHR">
         UN High Commissioner for Human Rights
        </a>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">
         <a href="#cite_note-49">
          [49]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Derechos_Human_Rights" title="Derechos Human Rights">
         Derechos Human Rights
        </a>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">
         <a href="#cite_note-50">
          [50]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Defend_International" title="Defend International">
         Defend International
        </a>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">
         <a href="#cite_note-51">
          [51]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">
         <a href="#cite_note-52">
          [52]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Front_Line_(NGO)" title="Front Line (NGO)">
         Front Line
        </a>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">
         <a href="#cite_note-53">
          [53]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">
         <a href="#cite_note-54">
          [54]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">

         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">
         <a href="#cite_note-56">
          [56]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/International_Federation_for_Human_Rights" title="International Federation for Human Rights">
         International Federation for Human Rights
        </a>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">
         <a href="#cite_note-57">
          [57]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">
         <a href="#cite_note-58">
          [58]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">
         <a href="#cite_note-59">
          [59]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">
         <a href="#cite_note-60">
          [60]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">
         <a href="#cite_note-61">
          [61]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Society_for_Threatened_Peoples" title="Society for Threatened Peoples">
         Society for Threatened Peoples
        </a>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">
         <a href="#cite_note-62">
          [62]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">
         <a href="#cite_note-63">
          [63]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_Refugee_Council" title="Norwegian Refugee Council">
         Norwegian Refugee Council
        </a>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">
         <a href="#cite_note-64">
          [64]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_human_rights_organisations" title="List of human rights organisations">
        List of human rights organisations
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/POLISARIO" title="POLISARIO">
        POLISARIO
       </a>
       has received criticism from the French organization
       <a class="external text" href="http://www.france-libertes.fr/" rel="nofollow">
        France Libertes
       </a>
       on its treatment of Moroccan prisoners of war,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">
        <a href="#cite_note-65">
         [65]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and on its general behaviour in the Tindouf refugee camps in reports by the
       <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">
        Belgian
       </a>
       commercial counseling society
       <a href="/wiki/European_strategic_intelligence_and_security_center" title="European strategic intelligence and security center">
        ESISC
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">
        <a href="#cite_note-66">
         [66]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">
        <a href="#cite_note-67">
         [67]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Social anthropologist of the Sahara Desert, Konstantina Isidoros, said that in both 2005 and 2008, ESISC issued two near-identical reports proclaiming distorted truths that Polisario is evolving to new fears terrorism, radical Islamism or international crime. According Isidoros "lies appear to play some peculiar importance in this report"
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">
        <a href="#cite_note-68">
         [68]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Jacob Mundi
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">
        <a href="#cite_note-69">
         [69]
        </a>
       </sup>
       considers this report as a part of the Moroccan propaganda designed to discredit the Polisario Front.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">
        <a href="#cite_note-70">
         [70]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       A number of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Polisario_defections" title="Polisario defections">
        former Polisario officials
       </a>
       who have defected to Morocco accuse the organisation of abuse of human rights and sequestration of the population in Tindouf.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">
        <a href="#cite_note-71">
         [71]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">
        <a href="#cite_note-72">
         [72]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>

      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Sahrawi_Arab_Democratic_Republic">

       </span>
      </h3>

        </i>

      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Moroccan_regions_and_provinces">
        Moroccan regions and provinces
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Three Moroccan regions are within or partly within Western Sahara:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Guelmim-Oued_Noun" title="Guelmim-Oued Noun">
         Guelmim-Oued Noun Region
        </a>
        <dl>
         <dd>
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/Assa-Zag_Province" title="Assa-Zag Province">
            Assa-Zag Province
           </a>
          </i>
         </dd>
        </dl>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/La%C3%A2youne-Sakia_El_Hamra" title="Laâyoune-Sakia El Hamra">
         Laâyoune-Sakia El Hamra Region
        </a>
        <dl>
         <dd>
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/Boujdour_Province" title="Boujdour Province">
            Boujdour Province
           </a>
          </i>
         </dd>
         <dd>
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/Es_Semara_Province" title="Es Semara Province">
            Es Semara Province
           </a>
          </i>
         </dd>
         <dd>
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/La%C3%A2youne_Province" title="Laâyoune Province">
            Laâyoune Province
           </a>
          </i>
         </dd>
         <dd>
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/Tarfaya_Province" title="Tarfaya Province">
            Tarfaya Province
           </a>
          </i>
         </dd>
        </dl>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Dakhla-Oued_Ed-Dahab" title="Dakhla-Oued Ed-Dahab">
         Dakhla-Oued Ed-Dahab Region
        </a>
        <dl>
         <dd>
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/Aousserd_Province" title="Aousserd Province">
            Aousserd Province
           </a>
          </i>
         </dd>
         <dd>
          <i>
           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oued_Eddahab_Province" title="Oued Eddahab Province">
            Oued Eddahab Province
           </a>
          </i>
         </dd>
        </dl>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       Morocco controls territory to the west of the berm (border wall) while the Sahrawi Republic controls territory to the east (see map on right).
      </p>
